
% Default to the notebook output style

    


% Inherit from the specified cell style.




    
\documentclass[11pt]{article}

    
    
    \usepackage[T1]{fontenc}
    % Nicer default font (+ math font) than Computer Modern for most use cases
    \usepackage{mathpazo}

    % Basic figure setup, for now with no caption control since it's done
    % automatically by Pandoc (which extracts ![](path) syntax from Markdown).
    \usepackage{graphicx}
    % We will generate all images so they have a width \maxwidth. This means
    % that they will get their normal width if they fit onto the page, but
    % are scaled down if they would overflow the margins.
    \makeatletter
    \def\maxwidth{\ifdim\Gin@nat@width>\linewidth\linewidth
    \else\Gin@nat@width\fi}
    \makeatother
    \let\Oldincludegraphics\includegraphics
    % Set max figure width to be 80% of text width, for now hardcoded.
    \renewcommand{\includegraphics}[1]{\Oldincludegraphics[width=.8\maxwidth]{#1}}
    % Ensure that by default, figures have no caption (until we provide a
    % proper Figure object with a Caption API and a way to capture that
    % in the conversion process - todo).
    \usepackage{caption}
    \DeclareCaptionLabelFormat{nolabel}{}
    \captionsetup{labelformat=nolabel}

    \usepackage{adjustbox} % Used to constrain images to a maximum size 
    \usepackage{xcolor} % Allow colors to be defined
    \usepackage{enumerate} % Needed for markdown enumerations to work
    \usepackage{geometry} % Used to adjust the document margins
    \usepackage{amsmath} % Equations
    \usepackage{amssymb} % Equations
    \usepackage{textcomp} % defines textquotesingle
    % Hack from http://tex.stackexchange.com/a/47451/13684:
    \AtBeginDocument{%
        \def\PYZsq{\textquotesingle}% Upright quotes in Pygmentized code
    }
    \usepackage{upquote} % Upright quotes for verbatim code
    \usepackage{eurosym} % defines \euro
    \usepackage[mathletters]{ucs} % Extended unicode (utf-8) support
    \usepackage[utf8x]{inputenc} % Allow utf-8 characters in the tex document
    \usepackage{fancyvrb} % verbatim replacement that allows latex
    \usepackage{grffile} % extends the file name processing of package graphics 
                         % to support a larger range 
    % The hyperref package gives us a pdf with properly built
    % internal navigation ('pdf bookmarks' for the table of contents,
    % internal cross-reference links, web links for URLs, etc.)
    \usepackage{hyperref}
    \usepackage{longtable} % longtable support required by pandoc >1.10
    \usepackage{booktabs}  % table support for pandoc > 1.12.2
    \usepackage[inline]{enumitem} % IRkernel/repr support (it uses the enumerate* environment)
    \usepackage[normalem]{ulem} % ulem is needed to support strikethroughs (\sout)
                                % normalem makes italics be italics, not underlines
    

    
    
    % Colors for the hyperref package
    \definecolor{urlcolor}{rgb}{0,.145,.698}
    \definecolor{linkcolor}{rgb}{.71,0.21,0.01}
    \definecolor{citecolor}{rgb}{.12,.54,.11}

    % ANSI colors
    \definecolor{ansi-black}{HTML}{3E424D}
    \definecolor{ansi-black-intense}{HTML}{282C36}
    \definecolor{ansi-red}{HTML}{E75C58}
    \definecolor{ansi-red-intense}{HTML}{B22B31}
    \definecolor{ansi-green}{HTML}{00A250}
    \definecolor{ansi-green-intense}{HTML}{007427}
    \definecolor{ansi-yellow}{HTML}{DDB62B}

    \definecolor{ansi-cyan-intense}{HTML}{258F8F}
    \definecolor{ansi-white}{HTML}{C5C1B4}
    \definecolor{ansi-white-intense}{HTML}{A1A6B2}

    % extracted from the output of `pandoc -s`
    \providecommand{\tightlist}{%
      \setlength{\itemsep}{0pt}\setlength{\parskip}{0pt}}

    % Add ',fontsize=\small' for more characters per line
    \newenvironment{Shaded}{}{}

    \newcommand{\NormalTok}[1]{{#1}}

    \newcommand{\ConstantTok}[1]{\textcolor[rgb]{0.53,0.00,0.00}{{#1}}}

    \newcommand{\OperatorTok}[1]{\textcolor[rgb]{0.40,0.40,0.40}{{#1}}}

\makeatletter
\def\PY@reset{\let\PY@it=\relax \let\PY@bf=\relax%
    \let\PY@ul=\relax \let\PY@tc=\relax%
    \let\PY@bc=\relax \let\PY@ff=\relax}
\def\PY@tok#1{\csname PY@tok@#1\endcsname}
\def\PY@toks#1+{\ifx\relax#1\empty\else%
    \PY@tok{#1}\expandafter\PY@toks\fi}
\def\PY@do#1{\PY@bc{\PY@tc{\PY@ul{%
    \PY@it{\PY@bf{\PY@ff{#1}}}}}}}
\def\PY#1#2{\PY@reset\PY@toks#1+\relax+\PY@do{#2}}

    Mission 1

  Create two imaginary datasets. One with a dictionnary and the other

{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}111}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} a) Create two imaginary datasets. One with a dictionnary and the other using lists}

    Mission 2

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  List all Nintendo Games published after 2010 for WIIU 
\item
  List all Video Games with Global Sales larger than the average 
\item
  List all Video Games with Global Sales larger than the average with a
  User and Critic score also higher than the average
\end{enumerate}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}125}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Before working with the database, we should first drop null values}

          \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{f}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{Global Sales mean is equal to: }\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}gsm:.3f\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)} 
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Calculate user score mean}

    Mission 3

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  Short the names of Publishers (ex. "Warner Bros. Interactive
  Entertainment" by "Warner Bros" ) 
\item
  List the sales of Nintendo Games grouped by year 
\item
  List sales grouped by Publisher and year 
\end{enumerate}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}146}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} a) Short the names of Publishers (ex. \PYZdq{}Warner Bros. Interactive Entertainment\PYZdq{} by \PYZdq{}Warner Bros\PYZdq{})}
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Also done for two other studios (\PYZdq{}Microsoft Game Studios\PYZdq{} to \PYZdq{}Microsoft\PYZdq{} and \PYZdq{}Sony Computer Entertainment\PYZdq{} to \PYZdq{}Sony\PYZdq{})}
          
          \PY{n}{vgs}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{Publisher}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{vgs}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{Publisher}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{replace}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{Warner Bros.     Mission 4

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  List the Publishers in the columns and the different sales in the rows
\item
  Count the number of game titles per publisher 
\item
  Display Platform in columns and sales in rows 
\end{enumerate}

    Mission 5

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  List sales (all) by year and by genre 
\item
  For the last 5 years, sales by platform and sales by publisher 
\item
  We want to explore a relationship between sales (all) and critic. 
\end{enumerate}

    Mission 6

For this and the next mission we will use data from Kaggle In concrete
from the World University Rankings Competition
https://www.kaggle.com/mylesoneill/world-university-rankings

In this first mission with the rankings we will focus on the Times
Ranking

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  Find the top 50 universities of the top 10 countries and see how do
  they compare. Are their rankings clustered? Are there very few good
  ones or there is a high dispersion. 
\end{enumerate}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}172}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Read university data }
          
          \PY{n}{uni} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pd}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{read\PYZus{}excel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{timesData.xlsx}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{country}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{year}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
The US seems to dominates the top 50 rankings, having the highest aggregate score and number of univeristies in the top 50.
However, of the universities in the top 50, the UK and Switzerland have a higher average score
All other countries have a couple of universities in the top 50, with an average score in the low 70s or high 60s
Finland is the only country with no universities in the top 50, indicating that their university scores are balanced


As we can see from the histogram below, most universities in the top 50 have a score around 50 or 60.
Very few universities actually have a score of 70 and above, the max being 95.2.

    \end{Verbatim}

    Mission 7

In this last mission we will compare two rankings: Shangai and Times.
The objective is to find out how well they correlate per country and
globally. We will use a sample and focus on the best 100 universities. 

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}173}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Load both datasets.}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pd}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{read\PYZus{}excel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{timesData.xlsx}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{country}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{year}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pd}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{read\PYZus{}excel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{shanghaiData.xlsx}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{year}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Convert total score on the times dataset to numeric}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pd}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{to\PYZus{}numeric}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{errors} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{coerce}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Drop null values from both datasets}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{dropna}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{inplace} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{dropna}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{inplace} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{)}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} First select the data for the same year in both tables. }
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Since the latest data on the shangai dataset is from 2015, this will be the year use for both datasets.}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t\PYZus{}2015} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{year}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{2015}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s\PYZus{}2015} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{year}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{2015}\PY{p}{]}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Select columns of interest (university\PYZus{}name, total\PYZus{}score and country in the times dataset)}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t\PYZus{}sel} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t\PYZus{}2015}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{country}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s\PYZus{}sel} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s\PYZus{}2015}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Merge both datasets, using the times dataset as the main one, since country data is available.}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}t\PYZus{}sel}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{merge}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}s\PYZus{}sel}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{how} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{left}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{on} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{columns} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{university\PYZus{}name}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{country}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}times}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}shangai}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Drop null values. }
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{dropna}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{inplace} \PY{o}{=} \PY{k+kc}{True}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{p}{]}
          
          \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}
          
          \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Some data has been lost, but we still have 60 entries of data, which is enough to run a correlation analysis.}
          
          \PY{n}{plot} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sns}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{jointplot}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{x} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}times}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{y} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}shangai}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{data} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{kind} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{reg}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{r} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{uni\PYZus{}both}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}times}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{total\PYZus{}score\PYZus{}shangai}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{corr}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{iloc}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}
          \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+se}{\PYZbs{}n}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{f}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{Correlation between the two datasets is positive and very strong: }\PY{l+s+si}{\PYZob{}r:.3f\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+s2}{This similarity indicates that while both rankings may have similarities in their approach}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s+se}{\PYZbs{}n}\PY{l+s+s2}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}
